Learning

(b) Why is β critical?
Without trend smoothing (β), simple exponential smoothing would systematically un-
derestimate a growing series. The β parameter captures the momentum of growth
by tracking how fast the level is increasing. For subscription services with consistent
growth, ignoring trend causes forecasts to always lag behind actuals, leading to poor
business planning for server capacity, marketing budgets, and staffing.

Q5(a)

two different machining methods. Both produce shafts with the same average diameter,
but the quality control engineer wants to determine which method has less variability. A
random sample of n1 = 10 shafts from Method A yields s1 = 0.032 mm; a sample of
n2 = 14 shafts from Method B gives s2 = 0.028 mm.
[5 Marks]
At the 5% level of significance, is there sufficient evidence to conclude that Method A
has greater variability than Method B?

SOLUTION

(a) H0: µHero = µTVS = µBajaj (no significant difference in mileages)
(b) H1: At least one brand has a different mean mileage.
(c) One-Way ANOVA (Analysis of Variance) — F -test.
(d) Parametric test — assumes normally distributed populations with equal variances.
(e) Critical region:

Interpretation: There is a very strong positive linear correlation (r = 0.990)
between average temperature and electricity usage in South Delhi. As temperatures
rise during summer months, electricity consumption increases sharply — almost
Integrated
Programmes
certainly due to air-conditioning and cooling loads. For urban energy planning, this
means demand spikes are highly predictable from temperature forecasts, enabling
Work
the grid to pre-position power reserves and prevent outages during extreme heat
events.

Work

α = 0.7 is more suitable for real-time AI applications with sudden demand
spikes. A higher α assigns more weight to recent observations, making the model
react quickly to sudden surges. α = 0.4 smooths more heavily and would lag behind
rapid changes — dangerous when under-provisioning cloud servers causes latency
in ML inference pipelines.

7.4. Question 3(b) — One-Sample Z-Test: Derm Assist Diagnosis
[2 Marks]
Time

Q3(b)

Programmes

Medi Scan AI claims its tool Derm Assist reduces average diagnosis time for high-
risk skin lesions by 20 minutes compared to standard care. A hospital tests it on 36
patients and finds a mean time reduction of 18.2 minutes, with a known population
standard deviation of 7.5 minutes.
As a data scientist, evaluate this claim at the 5% significance level. Formulate appropriate
hypotheses, perform the test, and interpret your conclusion in the context of clinical
deployment — considering both statistical evidence and the risk of decision errors.

Hypotheses (one-tailed, left — testing whether actual reduction falls below

Work

Fail to reject H0. At 5% significance level, there is insufficient evidence to
reject Medi Scan AI’s claim. The observed mean reduction of 18.2 min is not
statistically significantly less than the claimed 20 min.
Clinical context: While the test does not disprove the claim, the gap of 1.8 min
may still have clinical significance. A Type II error (failing to detect an under-
Integrated
performing tool) risks deploying an inadequate diagnostic tool. Regulators should
Programmes
consider a larger sample or tighter α before full clinical deployment.

Interpretation: For each additional litre of water per m2 per day, crop yield in-
creases by approximately 0.409 kg/m2. A garden receiving zero water would the-
oretically yield 0.607 kg/m2 (baseline). This model helps MUFI optimize irrigation
— avoiding over-watering (which causes nutrient leaching) and under-watering.

(c) Why GMM over single Gaussian?

peaks at 22 and 40 min) violates this assumption:

The series can be considered white noise: the mean is exactly zero, the values
show no persistent trend or pattern (alternating signs, no systematic runs), and the
series appears to fluctuate randomly around zero. Past residual values therefore
carry no predictive power for future values — confirming the forecasting model
has adequately captured the underlying signal.

(cid:136) Correlation (r) measures the strength and direction of the linear relationship be-
Work
tween two variables. It ranges from −1 to +1. Here r = −0.127 indicates a very
weak negative relationship — X and Y are essentially unrelated.

(cid:136) Regression quantifies the predictive relationship. It gives the best-fit line (OLS)
that minimises squared errors, telling us how Y changes per unit increase in X.
Used for forecasting and inference.

(cid:136) Together: correlation screens for relationships worth modelling; regression quan-
tifies and enables prediction. In ML: correlation aids feature selection; regression
provides the prediction model.

8.5. Question 3(a) — Time Series Forecasting: Simple Exponential
[5 Marks]
Smoothing

Q3(a)

For the month of March 2023, actual demand for a product is 250 units whereas the
forecast is 280 units. Is it possible to forecast the demand for the month of April 2023?
If possible, forecast for April 2023 using an appropriate time series model.

Programmes

Programmes

Programmes

Programmes

Learning

SOLUTION

Key Formulae

Simple Exponential Smoothing (SES):

Learning

Ft+1 = αAt + (1 − α)Ft

Learning

Integrated
Programmes
Work

Learning

where α ∈ (0, 1) is the smoothing constant, At = actual, Ft = forecast.

Integrated
Programmes
Work

Integrated
Programmes
Work

Integrated
Programmes
Work

Integrated
Programmes
Work

Integrated
Programmes
Work

Integrated
Programmes
Work

Programmes

Programmes

Learning

Learning

Yes, it is possible. With the March actual (A = 250) and March forecast (F = 280),
SES can generate an April forecast.
Using α = 0.5 (balanced weight):

Learning

Learning

Learning

Integrated
Programmes
Work

Integrated
Programmes
Work
Using α = 0.3 (more weight to history):

Learning

Learning

Learning

Integrated
Programmes
Work

FApril = 0.5(250) + 0.5(280) = 125 + 140 = 265 units

Learning

Integrated
Programmes
Work

FApril = 0.3(250) + 0.7(280) = 75 + 196 = 271 units

Using α = 0.7 (more weight to recent data):

Learning

Integrated
Programmes
Work

FApril = 0.7(250) + 0.3(280) = 175 + 84 = 259 units

Learning

Integrated
Programmes
Work

Learning

Integrated
Programmes
Work

SES is the most appropriate model when historical data is limited and no clear
trend or seasonality is evident. With α = 0.5: FApril = 265 units (recommended
balanced choice).

Step 3: Critical value: t0.05, 9 = 1.833 (one-tailed lower)
Rejection region: t < −1.833. Our tcalc = +3.953 is far from the rejection region.

Programmes

Programmes

Programmes

Learning

Fail to reject H0. The sample mean (125 months) is significantly above the
claimed minimum (120 months). At 5% significance, the manufacturer’s claim
that average life ≥ 120 months is validated. There is strong evidence the product
meets and exceeds its claimed minimum life.

Classification: Salaried (posterior score 0.090 vs 0 for Business).

Note: In practice, Laplace smoothing should be applied to avoid zero probabil-
ities from unseen feature-class combinations. With smoothing (+1 to each count,
vocabulary |V | = number of unique values per feature), the Business probability
would be non-zero but still much smaller than Salaried.

Total = 499, not 500. The discrepancy of 1 is due to rounding of continuous
probabilities to integers. There is no significant inconsistency in the data —
this is a standard artefact of rounding normal distribution probabilities.

(a) No. The sampling distribution of the mean does not follow a binomial distri-
bution. However, by the Central Limit Theorem (n = 45 ≥ 30), it approxi-
mately follows a Normal distribution.

(b) No. The sampling distribution does not follow a binomial distribution. With
n = 25 < 30, CLT does not strictly apply, but since the population is binomial
(discrete, not normal), the sampling distribution is approximately normal only for
large n.

(c) When the population itself is normally distributed, the sampling distri-
bution of the sample mean is exactly normally distributed for any sample
size n (including n = 9):

The Central Limit Theorem is not even needed here — normality of the sampling
distribution follows directly from the normality of the population.

Classification: SPAM.
All three words (“win”, “free”, “money”) appear exclusively in the Spam training
set. Even with Laplace smoothing, the Spam posterior is approximately 12×
higher than Ham. The message is classified as Spam.

Despite the DNA match, the probability of guilt is only 16.7%. This is the pros-
ecutor’s fallacy — confusing P (match | innocent) with P (innocent | match).
There are approximately 5 other people in the region who would also randomly
match the DNA, so the suspect is just 1 of 6 possible matches.

stolen, but only 1% of those with closed doors will have something stolen. If a garage is

Bayes’ theorem:

P (Open | Robbed) =

0.02

=

0.0125
0.02

= 0.625

Programmes

If a garage is robbed, the probability the door was left open is 0.625 = 62.5%.
Despite open garages being only 25% of all garages, they account for 62.5% of
robberies — a 2.5× overrepresentation, confirming that open doors significantly
increase theft risk.

The Poisson approximation is close to the Binomial result. The approximation
works reasonably well here, though p = 0.2 is not very small (Poisson is most
accurate when p < 0.1 and n > 30), which explains the small discrepancy of ≈ 3%.

WBN is approximately symmetric; the remaining datasets are positively skewed, with
frequencies concentrated toward the lower (left) end.
Inference 3 — Outlier Detection (1.5 (cid:214) IQR Rule):
For HIV: IQR = 170 − 90 = 80; fences = [90 − 120, 170 + 120] = [−30, 290]
Maximum = 360 > 290 ⇒ potential upper outlier in HIV
For WBN: IQR = 70 − 25 = 45; fences = [−42.5, 137.5] — no outliers
For BNC: IQR = 115 − 90 = 25; fences = [52.5, 152.5] — Max=180 is a potential outlier
For HBCN: IQR = 63 − 30 = 33; fences = [−19.5, 112.5] — no outliers

Independent events: P (A∩B) = P (A)·P (B)
P (Ac ∩ B) = P (B) − P (A ∩ B)

Mutually exclusive: P (A∩B) = 0

Integrated
Programmes
Work

(a) Statement: P (A ∪ B) = 0?
Since A and B are independent:

Integrated
Programmes
Work
P (A ∪ B) = P (A) + P (B) − P (A ∩ B) = 0.35 + 0.30 − 0.105 = 0.545

Integrated
Programmes
Work
P (A ∩ B) = P (A) · P (B) = 0.35 × 0.30 = 0.105

Integrated
Programmes
Work

Learning

Learning

Learning

Programmes

Learning

Integrated
Statement (a) is INCORRECT. P (A ∪ B) = 0.545 ̸= 0. Independence means
Programmes
the occurrence of one event does not affect the other — it does not mean the union
Work
is zero.

(b) Statement: P (A ∩ B) = 0 as they are mutually exclusive?

P (A ∩ B) = P (A) · P (B) = 0.105 ̸= 0

Integrated

Statement (b) is INCORRECT. Two independent events (both with non-zero
probability) cannot be mutually exclusive. Mutual exclusion requires P (A∩B) = 0,
but independence gives P (A∩B) = P (A)·P (B) = 0.105 > 0. These two properties
are contradictory for non-trivial events.

P (Ac ∩ B) = P (Ac) · P (B) = 0.65 × 0.30 = 0.195

Continuity correction: P (a < X < b) ≈ P (a + 0.5 < Xc < b − 0.5)

Since µ = 30 and σ ≈ 4.9, the range (50, 80) is more than 4 standard deviations
above the mean. The probability is essentially zero — it is extremely unlikely for
a Binomial(150, 0.2) variable to exceed 50, let alone 80.

Note: The Z-table only goes up to Z ≈ 4, beyond which Φ(Z) ≈ 1. Both standard-
ized values (4.18 and 10.10) are in this region, so P ≈ Φ(10.10) − Φ(4.18) ≈ 0.

It is observed that the average amount of time a customer spends in a supermarket is 40
minutes with a standard deviation of 5 minutes. Find the probability that the sampling
distribution of the mean time lies between 35 and 45 minutes, where the sample size is
[3 Marks]
50.

innovateachievelead

Since Z = ±7.07 is far beyond the table range (±4), both tails are essentially 0:

P (−7.07 < Z < 7.07) ≈ 1 − 0 = 1.00

Programmes

P (35 < ¯X < 45) ≈ 1.00 = 100%
The interval [35, 45] is ±7 standard errors from the mean. By the Z-table, values
beyond ±4 approach 0 and ±4 approaches 1. Therefore the entire probability mass
lies within this interval — it is virtually certain the sample mean will fall between
35 and 45 minutes.

Verifying a PDF: Given f (x), differentiate F (x) to confirm F ′(x) = f (x).
Finding Mode (Max of PDF): Set f ′(x) = 0, solve for x, confirm f ′′(x) < 0.

Y = ln X — stabilises variance, normalises right-skewed distributions

(lognormal distribution mean)

One-Way ANOVA tests whether the means of 3 or more groups are equal, where
groups differ by one factor (independent variable).
H0 : µ1 = µ2 = · · · = µk

H1 : At least one mean differs

Three motorcycle brands — Hero, TVS, Bajaj — are tested for mileage (km/L).
Hero: 60, 65, 65, 63, 62 TVS: 70, 75, 78, 56, 52 Bajaj: 85, 77, 65, 53, 82
At α = 0.05, test whether there is a significant difference in mean mileages.

¯xB = (85 + 77 + 65 + 53 + 82)/5 = 362/5 = 72.4

k = 3 groups, ni = 5 each, N = 15
Group means: ¯xH = (60 + 65 + 65 + 63 + 62)/5 = 315/5 = 63
56 + 52)/5 = 331/5 = 66.2
Grand mean: ¯¯x = (315 + 331 + 362)/15 = 1008/15 = 67.2
SS Between: SSB = 5(63 − 67.2)2 + 5(66.2 − 67.2)2 + 5(72.4 − 67.2)2 = 5(17.64) +
5(1.00) + 5(27.04) = 88.2 + 5.0 + 135.2 = 228.4

Integrated

Work

Observation 1 — Outliers Present: Features like horsepower (48–288), engine size
(61–326), curb weight (1488–4066), and compression ratio (7–23) show very large
gaps between min and max relative to their means. This indicates likely outliers requiring
detection and handling during preprocessing.
Observation 2 — Different Scales (Normalization Required): curb weight ≈
2555, engine size ≈ 127, city mpg ≈ 25, symboling ≈ 0.83. Since scales differ drasti-
cally, algorithms like KNN, SVM, and neural networks require standardization or min-
max normalization before training.
Observation 3 — Right Skewness: horsepower: mean = 104.2 > median = 95;
engine size: mean = 126.9 > median = 120; curb weight: mean = 2555 > median
= 2414. These are right-skewed — log or Box-Cox transformations may be needed.
Observation 4 — No Missing Values: All features show count = 205, so no impu-
tation is required — the dataset is complete.

BIRLA INSTITUTE OF TECHNOLOGY & SCIENCE, PILANI
Work Integrated Learning Programmes · ISM AIMLCZC418

innovateachievelead

SOLUTION

1. Measures of Central Tendency (Mean, Median, Mode):
Identify the centre.
Comparing mean vs median reveals skewness — mean ≫ median implies right-skewed
data with outliers.
2. Measures of Variability (Std Dev, IQR, Range): Quantify spread. Large std dev
indicates wide variation needing normalization. IQR is robust to outliers and used in the
1.5×IQR outlier detection rule.
3. Outlier Detection: Using IQR fences or Z-scores (|Z| > 3), extreme values are
flagged. Outliers distort model training and must be removed, capped, or transformed
before fitting ML models.

Let A, B and C are three events such that P (A) = 0.26, P (B) = 0.36, P (C) = 0.48,
P (A ∩ B) = 0.03, P (B ∩ C) = 0.05, P (A ∩ C) = 0.04 and P (A ∩ B ∩ C) = 0.01.
Find P (A ∩ Bc), P (Ac ∩ B), P (Ac ∪ Bc ∪ C c), P (A only), P (B only), and P (C only).

Learning

P (A ∩ Bc) = P (A) − P (A ∩ B) = 0.26 − 0.03 = 0.23
P (Ac ∩ B) = P (B) − P (A ∩ B) = 0.36 − 0.03 = 0.33
P (Ac ∪ Bc ∪ C c) = 1 − P (A ∩ B ∩ C) = 1 − 0.01 = 0.99
Integrated
P (A only) = 0.26 − 0.03 − 0.04 + 0.01 = 0.20
Programmes

A2.10 — Validate Statement: Mutually Exclusive vs Independent [3M] (Mul-
tiple exams)

Integrated
Programmes
Work

Integrated
Programmes
Work

Programmes

Validate the following statement with logic and examples in support:

“If two events are mutually exclusive, then they are independent also and vice versa.”

Learning

Integrated
Programmes
Work

Integrated

Learning

SOLUTION

Learning

Learning

Learning

Integrated
The statement is FALSE.
Programmes
Mutually exclusive means P (A ∩ B) = 0. For independence we need P (A ∩ B) =
Work
P (A) · P (B).
If P (A ∩ B) = 0 and P (A) > 0, P (B) > 0, then P (A) · P (B) > 0 ̸= 0. So mutually
exclusive events with non-zero probability are always dependent.
Example: Die roll: A = {1, 2, 3}, B = {4, 5, 6}. P (A ∩ B) = 0 (mutually exclusive),
but P (A) · P (B) = 0.5 × 0.5 = 0.25 ̸= 0. Not independent.

Integrated
Programmes
Work

Integrated
Programmes
Work

Learning

Learning

Learning

Learning

Programmes

Integrated
Programmes
Work

Integrated
Programmes
Work

Integrated
Programmes
Work

Learning

Integrated

Mutually exclusive events (non-zero probability) are always dependent, not in-
dependent.

Comparison: Poisson overestimates (0.0127 ≫ 0.00129). Poisson approximates bino-
mial well only when n is large and p is very small (p ≤ 0.1). Here p = 0.6 is large,
making Poisson inappropriate. Binomial is correct here.

BIRLA INSTITUTE OF TECHNOLOGY & SCIENCE, PILANI
Work Integrated Learning Programmes · ISM AIMLCZC418

innovateachievelead

α = 0.7 is more suitable for real-time AI applications with sudden de-
mand spikes.
A higher α gives more weight to the most recent actual observation, making the
model react faster to sudden changes. With α = 0.4, the forecast is smoother but
lags behind sharp movements; with α = 0.7, the model adapts quickly — essential
for cloud autoscaling where delayed response causes service degradation or cost
overruns.

Part (ii) — Model Appropriateness:

Integrated
Programmes
Work

Learning
The positive slope ( ˆβ1 = 0.409) shows yield increases with water input, and
the relationship appears approximately linear across the observed range (2.0–6.0
L/m†/day). However, real plant physiology suggests a diminishing-returns curve:
beyond an optimal point, over-irrigation causes waterlogging and nutrient leach-
ing. The linear model is reasonable as a local approximation but may overestimate
yield at very high water inputs. A quadratic model (Y = β0 + β1X + β2X 2) would
better capture the inverted-U response.

Part (iii) — Optimal Water Input Range:

Using the linear model, the predicted yields at key levels are:

X = 3.0 : ˆY = 0.608 + 0.409(3.0) = 1.83 kg/m2

Programmes

X = 4.0 : ˆY = 0.608 + 0.409(4.0) = 2.24 kg/m2
X = 5.0 : ˆY = 0.608 + 0.409(5.0) = 2.65 kg/m2

Programmes

Programmes

Learning

Integrated
Programmes
Work

Learning

Learning

Water-use efficiency (WUE) = Y /X peaks in the lower range where each additional
litre produces the highest yield gain. Given Mumbai’s water scarcity and real
data showing diminishing returns beyond ≈ 5 L/m†/day:
Recommended optimal range: 3.5–4.5 L/m†/day. This range delivers good
yield (≈ 2.0–2.5 kg/m†) while conserving water, balancing productivity and sus-
tainability for rooftop urban farming.

Part (c) — Why GMM over single Gaussian?

Learning

Integrated
Programmes
Work

Learning

Integrated
Programmes
Work

Learning

Integrated
Programmes
Work

Learning

A single Gaussian assumes a unimodal, symmetric distribution. Bimodal data
(with two peaks at 22 and 40 min) cannot be well-described by a single Gaussian —
it would produce a poor fit with high variance and misleading probability estimates
Integrated
in the valley between the two groups. A GMM explicitly models the two sub-
Programmes
populations, capturing both modes correctly and providing interpretable mixing
Work
weights (proportion of quick vs. leisurely eaters).

Part (b) — White Noise Test: Series: {2, −1, 0, 1, −2, 1, −1, 0}, n = 8

Key Formulae

White noise requires: (1) E[εt] = 0, (2) Var(εt) = σ2 (constant), (3) No autocorre-
lation: Cov(εt, εt−k) = 0 ∀ k ̸= 0.

(cid:136) Variance = 1.714 — appears constant across the series ✓

(cid:136) Autocorrelation: A formal Ljung-Box test would be needed for rigor, but
for 8 observations, the series shows no obvious systematic pattern — it oscil-
lates irregularly with no trend or periodicity.

Learning

Learning

Learning

Integrated
Programmes
Work

Conclusion: With mean = 0 and no visible autocorrelation structure, the series
can tentatively be considered white noise. A forecasting model whose residu-
als exhibit these properties is well-specified (the model has captured all systematic
information from the data).

Fail to reject H0.
Work
At the 5% significance level, there is no statistically significant difference in the
vaccination proportions between City A (60%) and City B (54%). The observed
difference of 6 percentage points could plausibly be due to sampling variation alone.
Integrated
Programmes
Public Health Implication: Both campaigns achieved comparable uptake. Pol-
icymakers should consider whether practical significance (a 6% gap) warrants fur-
Work
ther investigation, even if statistical significance was not reached. A larger sample
size would provide greater power to detect smaller real differences.

Cluster 1: Holt’s Double Exponential Smoothing (Time
Series with Trend)

Key Formulae

Holt’s Method (Two-Parameter Exponential Smoothing):

Programmes

Programmes

Learning

Lt = αYt + (1 − α)(Lt−1 + Tt−1)
Tt = β(Lt − Lt−1) + (1 − β)Tt−1

Integrated
Programmes
Work

Ft+h = Lt + h · Tt

F7 = L6 + T6 = 199.87 + 16.24 = 216.11

Integrated
Programmes
Work

Holt’s method is more appropriate. The dataset has a clear, consistent upward
trend (≈ 15 units/month). SES gives F7 = 184.60, consistently lagging behind
actuals because it has no trend component. Holt’s method gives F7 = 216.11,
tracking the trend closely. For any trending series, SES will perpetually under-
forecast.

Week 9 forecast: 57.67 hundred visitors. Regarding order k: a smaller k (e.g.,
k = 2) responds faster to changes but retains more noise; a larger k (e.g., k = 5)
produces smoother forecasts but lags more, losing recent signals. Choose k based
on the volatility of the series.

17.1. Predicted Q12 — GMM: Server Response Times

[5 Marks]

PQ12 — Two-Component GMM: Cloud Server Response Time

A cloud monitoring system observes that server response times (ms) are bimodal. A
2-component GMM with equal mixing weights (π1 = π2 = 0.5) is fitted:

(cid:136) E-step (Expectation): For each observed response time xi, compute the
responsibility rk(xi) — the probability that observation i was generated by
component k. This is a “soft assignment”: each server request is fractionally
attributed to both components proportionally to their likelihood.

. This maximises the expected log-likelihood from the E-step.

The patient with 7-day recovery time is assigned to Group 1 (Minor Surgery)
with 97.95% posterior probability. Despite the mixing weight (π1 = 0.6), the
classification is overwhelmingly determined by proximity to µ1 = 5 days vs the
distance from µ2 = 15 days.

The EM algorithm is guaranteed to increase the log-likelihood at each step but
only converges to a local maximum because:

Integrated
Programmes
(cid:136) The GMM log-likelihood surface is non-convex with multiple peaks.
Work
(cid:136) The final solution depends on initialisation — different starting values for

Integrated
Programmes
Work

Integrated
Programmes
Work

µk, σ2

k, πk lead to different local optima.

Integrated
Programmes
(cid:136) Mitigation: Run EM multiple times with random initialisations (multi-
Work
start) and select the solution with highest log-likelihood, or use K-Means to
initialise cluster centres.

fX|Y (x | y) = e−x = fX(x) — the conditional distribution of X given Y does not
Integrated
depend on y.
Programmes
X and Y are independent. We can verify: fX(x) · fY (y) = e−x · 2e−2y =
2e−x−2y = f (x, y). The joint PDF factors perfectly, confirming independence.

Critical values: F0.05(1, 2) = 18.51; F0.05(2, 2) = 19.00

Neither Frow = 0.80 nor Fcol = 1.03 exceeds its critical value. Fail to reject H0
for both factors. With only 6 observations, the experiment is underpowered.
More replicates per cell would be needed to detect significant effects.

Only 16.2% of patients who test positive actually have the disease.
Clinical implication: Despite high sensitivity (95%) and specificity (90%), the
very low prevalence (2%) means that most positives are false alarms. For every
100 positive tests, only ≈ 16 patients truly have the disease. This has major
implications:

Work

(cid:136) Using the AI tool only on high-risk subpopulations (higher prevalence) would

dramatically improve the PPV.

Learning

Reject H0. At the 5% significance level, Agile methodology significantly reduces
project completion time compared to Waterfall (t = −2.296, df = 20, p < 0.05).
The Agile team completes projects on average 3.6 days faster. Given the variabil-
ity in both teams (pooled sp ≈ 3.66 days), this difference is statistically meaningful
and supports adopting Agile for time-sensitive data science projects.
